(Chang 1984) conjectures that the termination -b is original. This verb is frequently added to nouns to form new verbs, it generally indicates a voluntary verb, whereas {འཐེབས} is used in the same way to indicate lack of volition or to show that the action was well done (Chang 1984).

ཧལ	Present: {ཧལ} CD, DS, TC. \nPast: {ཧལ} [DS].\nFuture: {ཧལ} [DS].\nInvoluntary: (Hoshi 2003).\nIntransitive: DS.\nMeaning: To pant, wheeze, snort (Ja) CD. To have rough, short breath with the mouth open DS. (dialect) To breath with difficulty TC.\nNote: perhaps onomatopoeic

ཧྲག	Present: {ཧྲག} CD. \nInvoluntary: (Hoshi 2003).\nMeaning: To require more and more (Ja) CD. To be highly efficient (Hoshi 2003).
ཧྲད	Present: {ཧྲད} CD. \nMeaning: 1. To thrust, to push violently, to stem firmly. 2. To scratch. 3. To exert one's self (Ja) CD.\nNote: Compare {འདྲད}.
